<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation,_Jeddah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg/220px-Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg/330px-Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg/440px-Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation%2C_Jeddah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1240" data-file-height="933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation,_Jeddah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Organisation of Islamic Cooperation Head-office Building, Jeddah</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</b> (<b>OIC</b>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">منظمة التعاون الإسلامي</span>&#8206;; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation de la coopération islamique</i>) is an international organization founded in 1969, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Member states of the Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">57 member states</a>, with a collective population of over 1.8 billion as of 2015 with 53 countries being Muslim-majority countries. The organisation states that it is "the collective voice of the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>" and works to "safeguard and protect the interests of the Muslim world in the spirit of promoting international peace and harmony".<sup id="cite_ref-EIMW_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIMW-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The OIC has permanent delegations to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The official languages of the OIC are Arabic, English, and French.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Al-Aqsa_fire">Al-Aqsa fire</span></h3>
<p>On 21 August 1969 a fire was started in the <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">Al-Aqsa Mosque</a> in Jerusalem.  <a href="/wiki/Amin_al-Husseini" title="Amin al-Husseini">Amin al-Husseini</a>, the former Mufti of Jerusalem, called the arson a "Jewish crime" and called for all Muslim heads of state to convene a summit.<sup id="cite_ref-ECSWWII_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECSWWII-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>  (The fire, which "destroyed part of the old wooden roof and a 800-year-old pulpit"<sup id="cite_ref-LIEBER-2017_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIEBER-2017-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> was blamed on the mental illness of the perpetrator — Australian Christian fundamentalist <a href="/wiki/Denis_Michael_Rohan" title="Denis Michael Rohan">Denis Michael Rohan</a> — by Israel, and on <a href="/wiki/Denis_Michael_Rohan#Arab.2FMuslim_reactions" title="Denis Michael Rohan">Zionists and Zionism</a> in general by the Islamic conference.)<sup id="cite_ref-elibrary_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elibrary-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_Conference">Islamic Conference</span></h3>
<p>On 25 September 1969, an Islamic Conference, a summit of representatives of 24 Muslim majority countries (most of the representatives being heads of state), was held in <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a>, Morocco.<sup id="cite_ref-ECSWWII_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECSWWII-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EIMW_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIMW-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> A resolution was passed stating that 
</p>
<blockquote><p>"Muslim government would consult with a view to promoting among themselves close cooperation and mutual assistance in the economic, scientific, cultural and spiritual fields, inspired by the immortal teachings of Islam."<sup id="cite_ref-ECSWWII_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECSWWII-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Six months later in March 1970, the First Islamic Conference of Foreign Ministers was held in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-elibrary_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elibrary-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
In 1972, the Organisation of the Islamic Conference (OIC, now the Organisation of Islamic Cooperation) was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-esposito-1998-164_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esposito-1998-164-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">al-Aqsa</a> fire is regarded as one of the catalysts for the formation of the OIC,  many <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> have aspired to a pan-Islamic institution that would serve the common political, economic, and social interests of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ummah" title="Ummah">ummah</a></i> (Muslim community) since the 19th century. In particular, the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> left a vacuum.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goals">Goals</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_OIC.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_OIC.svg/200px-Flag_of_OIC.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_OIC.svg/300px-Flag_of_OIC.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_OIC.svg/400px-Flag_of_OIC.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_OIC.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old flag of the OIC</div></div></div>
<p>According to its charter, the OIC aims to preserve Islamic social and economic values; promote solidarity amongst member states; increase cooperation in social, economic, cultural, scientific, and political areas; uphold international peace and security; and advance education, particularly in the fields of science and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-EIMW_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIMW-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The emblem of the OIC contains three main elements that reflect its vision and mission as incorporated in its new Charter. These elements are: the <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a>, the Globe, and the Crescent.
</p><p>On 5 August 1990, 45 foreign ministers of the OIC adopted the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Declaration_on_Human_Rights_in_Islam" title="Cairo Declaration on Human Rights in Islam">Cairo Declaration on Human Rights in Islam</a> to serve as a guidance for the member states in the matters of human rights in as much as they are compatible with the <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a>, or Quranic Law.<sup id="cite_ref-CDHRII_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDHRII-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2008, the OIC conducted a formal revision of its charter.  The revised charter set out to promote human rights, fundamental freedoms, and good governance in all member states. The revisions also removed any mention of the Cairo Declaration on Human Rights in Islam.  Within the revised charter, the OIC has chosen to support the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a> and international law, without mentioning the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugees">Refugees</span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, OIC countries hosted 18 million refugees by the end of 2010. Since then OIC members have absorbed refugees from other conflicts, including <a href="/wiki/Syrian_uprising_(2011%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian uprising (2011–present)">the uprising in Syria</a>. In May 2012, the OIC addressed these concerns at the "Refugees in the Muslim World" conference in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_name_and_emblem">New name and emblem</span></h3>
<p>On 28 June 2011 during the 38th Council of Foreign Ministers meeting (CFM) in Astana, Kazakhstan, the organisation changed its name from <b>Organisation of the Islamic Conference</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">منظمة المؤتمر الإسلامي</span>&#8206;; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation de la Conférence Islamique</i>) to its current name.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The OIC also changed its logo at this time.
</p>

<div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OIC_Diagram-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A clickable <a href="/wiki/Euler_diagram" title="Euler diagram">Euler diagram</a> showing the relationships between various multinational organisations within the <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (note that Syria is currently suspended from all organizations included in this diagram due to <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_abuses" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights abuses">human rights abuses</a> in the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>).<span style="float:right; font-weight:normal; font-size:xx-small;"><a href="/wiki/Template:Supranational_Islamic_Bodies" title="Template:Supranational Islamic Bodies"><span title="View this emplate">v</span></a> &#x2022; <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Supranational_Islamic_Bodies" title="Template talk:Supranational Islamic Bodies"><span title="Discuss this template">d</span></a> &#x2022; <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Supranational_Islamic_Bodies&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style=";">e</span></a> </span></div></div></div>
<p>The Organisation of Islamic Cooperation has 57 members, 56 of which are also <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states of the United Nations</a>, the exception being <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>. Some members, especially in West Africa and South America, are – though with large Muslim populations – not necessarily <a href="/wiki/Muslim_majority_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim majority countries">Muslim majority countries</a>. A few countries with significant Muslim populations, such as <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, sit as Observer States.
</p><p>The collective <a href="/wiki/List_of_OIC_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of OIC countries by population">population of OIC member states</a> is over 1.9 billion as of 2018.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Positions">Positions</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Union_of_the_OIC_Member_States" title="Parliamentary Union of the OIC Member States">Parliamentary Union of the OIC Member States</a> (PUOICM) was established in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> in 1999, and its head office is situated in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>. Only OIC members are entitled to membership in the union.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 June 2007, then-United States President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> announced that the United States would establish an envoy to the OIC. Bush said of the envoy, "Our special envoy will listen to and learn from representatives from Muslim states, and will share with them America's views and values."<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> As of June 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Arsalan Suleman is acting special envoy. He was appointed on 13 February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In an investigation of the accuracy of a series of chain emails, <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a> reported that during the October 2003&#160;&#8211;&#32;April 2004 session of the General Assembly, 17 individual members of the OIC voted against the United States 88% of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The OIC, on 28 March 2008, joined the criticism of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Fitna_(film)" title="Fitna (film)">Fitna</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> lawmaker <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, which features disturbing images of violent acts juxtaposed with alleged verses from the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, the OIC announced its support for the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Zaidiyyah" title="Zaidiyyah">Shia Houthis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Israeli.E2.80.93Palestinian_conflict"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli–Palestinian_conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</span></h3>
<p>The OIC supports a <a href="/wiki/Two-state_solution" title="Two-state solution">two-state solution</a> to the Israeli–Palestinian conflict.
</p><p>The OIC has called for  boycott of Israeli products in effort to pressure Israel into ending the occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There was a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> in 2013. Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ekmeleddin_Ihsanoglu" class="mw-redirect" title="Ekmeleddin Ihsanoglu">Ekmeleddin Ihsanoglu</a> said that foreign ministers would discuss the possibility of cutting ties with any state that recognised Jerusalem as the capital of Israel or that moves its embassy to its environs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2017, the extraordinary meeting held to response Donald Trump's decision on recognizing Jerusalem, resulting "Istanbul Declaration on Freedom for Al Quds."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2019, the OIC condemned <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>'s plans to <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annex</a> the eastern portion of the occupied <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley" title="Jordan Valley">Jordan Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_India">Relationship with India</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_India" title="Islam in India">Islam in India</a></div>
<p>Islam is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_India" title="Religion in India">religion in India</a> after <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, with roughly 15% of the country's population or 201 million people identifying as adherents of Islam (2018 estimate).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It makes India the country with the largest Muslim population outside Muslim-majority countries. However, <a href="/wiki/India%E2%80%93Pakistan_relations" title="India–Pakistan relations">India's relationship with Pakistan</a> has always been tense and has a direct impact on India-OIC relations, with Pakistan being a founding member of the OIC. India has pushed for the OIC to accept India as a member, arguing that about 11% of all Muslims worldwide live in India. Pakistan opposes India's entry into the OIC.<sup id="cite_ref-ArabNews20110630_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArabNews20110630-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The reason for opposition to India's entry into the OIC cited by Pakistan is due to the human rights issues and problems faced by the <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir#Demographics" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Kashmiris</a> in the <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">Indian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> India has pushed against the OIC for referring to the state of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a> as "occupied by India".<sup id="cite_ref-ArabNews20110630_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArabNews20110630-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Muslim world has been supporting Pakistan rather than India in case of dissentions between the two. However, the role of the OIC concerning the <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Insurgency in Jammu and Kashmir">Kashmir issue</a> is that India has the largest Muslim minority and those people have shown desire to join the OIC. While the First Islamic Summit held in 1969 in <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a> did not have the issue of the Kashmir people, granting the 60 million Muslims living in India membership in the OIC was discussed. The head of the Indian delegation, the then ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, even addressed the gathering. While General <a href="/wiki/Yahya_Khan" title="Yahya Khan">Yahya Khan</a> of Pakistan did agree, he showed his extreme displeasure at the induction of non muslim representative.  <a href="/wiki/Fakhruddin_Ali_Ahmed" title="Fakhruddin Ali Ahmed">Fakhruddin Ali Ahmad</a>, who was to head the Indian delegation was on his way to Rabata. Yahya Khan took a stand against India and threatened to boycott summit which caused a major controversy. As such Indo-Pak differences led Islamabad to keep India out for the final session of the 1969 conference and all summits thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/2019_Pulwama_attack" title="2019 Pulwama attack">A suicide attack on Indian Forces</a> on 14 February 2019, followed by <a href="/wiki/2019_Balakot_airstrike" title="2019 Balakot airstrike">Indian Air Strikes</a> subsequently led to <a href="/wiki/2019_India%E2%80%93Pakistan_standoff" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 India–Pakistan standoff">a military stand off</a> between India and Pakistan.
</p><p>Indian Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Sushma_Swaraj" title="Sushma Swaraj">Sushma Swaraj</a> was invited in OIC.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Pakistan rejected this development and demanded the expulsion of India from the summit citing Kashmir issue and Indian violation of airspace of Pakistan, while India has stated that it has proofs for its strikes in the form of SAR imagery.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> OIC called emergency meeting of Kashmir contact group on Pakistan's request, the meeting was held on 26 February 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> OIC advised restraint to Pakistan and India.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the first time in five decades, the United Arab Emirates invited <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_External_Affairs_(India)" title="Minister of External Affairs (India)">foreign minister of India</a> <a href="/wiki/Sushma_Swaraj" title="Sushma Swaraj">Sushma Swaraj</a> to attend the inaugural plenary 46th meeting of OIC foreign ministers held in Abu Dhabi on 1 and 2 March overruling strong objections by Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> boycotted the meet objecting to the invitation to India. Swaraj addressed the meet raising concern for spreading terrorism.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cartoons_of_Muhammad">Cartoons of Muhammad</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jyllands-Posten_Muhammad_cartoons_controversy" title="Jyllands-Posten Muhammad cartoons controversy">Jyllands-Posten Muhammad cartoons controversy</a></div>
<p>Cartoons of Muhammad, published in a Danish newspaper in September 2005, were found offensive by a number of Muslims. <a href="/wiki/Third_Extraordinary_Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference" title="Third Extraordinary Session of the Islamic Summit Conference">Third Extraordinary Session of the Islamic Summit Conference</a> in December 2005 condemned publication of the cartoons, resulting in broader coverage of the issue by news media in Muslim countries. Subsequently, violent demonstrations throughout the Islamic world resulted in several deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<p>OIC created the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Declaration_on_Human_Rights_in_Islam" title="Cairo Declaration on Human Rights in Islam">Cairo Declaration on Human Rights in Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CDHRII_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDHRII-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> While proponents claim it is not an alternative to the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">UDHR</a>, but rather complementary to it, Article 24 states that "all the rights and freedoms stipulated in this Declaration are subject to the Islamic Shari'ah" and Article 25 follows with "the Islamic Shari'ah is the only source of reference for the explanation or clarification of any of the articles of this Declaration." Attempts to have it adopted by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> have met increasing criticism, because of its contradiction of the UDHR, including from liberal Muslim groups.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Critics of the CDHR state bluntly that it is "manipulation and hypocrisy," "designed to dilute, if not altogether eliminate, civil and political rights protected by international law" and attempts to "circumvent these principles [of freedom and equality]."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> says that OIC has "fought doggedly" and successfully within the United Nations Human Rights Council to shield states from criticism, except when it comes to <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Criticism of Israel">criticism of Israel</a>. For example, when independent experts reported violations of human rights in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a>, "state after state from the OIC took the floor to denounce the experts for daring to look beyond Israeli violations to discuss <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>'s as well." OIC demands that the council "should work cooperatively with abusive governments rather than condemn them." HRW responds that this works with those who are willing to cooperate; others exploit the passivity.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The OIC has been criticised for failing to discuss the treatment of ethnic minorities within member countries, such as the oppression of the <a href="/wiki/Kurds_in_Syria" title="Kurds in Syria">Kurds in Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurds_in_Turkey" title="Kurds in Turkey">Turkey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ahwaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahwaz">Ahwaz</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hazaras" title="Hazaras">Hazaras</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, the '<a href="/wiki/Al-Akhdam" title="Al-Akhdam">Al-Akhdam</a>' in <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Along with the revisions of the OIC's charter in 2008, the member states created the Independent Permanent Human Rights Commission (IPHRC). The IPHRC is an advisory body, independent from the OIC, composed of eighteen individuals from a variety of educational and professional backgrounds. The IPHRC has the power to monitor human rights within the member states and facilitates the integration of human rights into all OIC mandates.  The IPHRC also aids in the promotion of political, civil, and economic rights in all member states.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2017, the Independent Human Rights Commission (IPHRC) of the OIC strongly condemned the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_persecution_in_Myanmar_(2016%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohingya persecution in Myanmar (2016–present)">human rights violations</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya Muslims</a> in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2018, the OIC raised the issue of <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">China</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps" title="Xinjiang re-education camps">Xinjiang re-education camps</a> and human rights abuses against the <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghur</a> <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Muslim</a> minority.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_at_the_United_Nations" title="LGBT rights at the United Nations">LGBT rights at the United Nations</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_in_Islam" title="LGBT in Islam">LGBT in Islam</a></div>
<p>In March 2012, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> held its first discussion of <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> and gender identity, following the 2011 passage of a resolution supporting LGBT rights proposed by the Republic of South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Pakistan's representative addressed the session on behalf of the OIC, denouncing the discussion and questioning the concept of sexual orientation, which he said was being used to promote "licentious behaviour&#160;... against the fundamental teachings of various religions, including Islam". He stated that the council should not discuss the topic again. Most Arab countries and some African ones later walked out of the session.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nonetheless, OIC members <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> have signed <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_at_the_United_Nations" title="LGBT rights at the United Nations">a UN Declaration supporting LGBT rights in the General Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Whilst <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> had legalized homosexuality.
</p><p>In May 2016, 57 countries including <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> from the Organization of Islamic Cooperation requested the removal of <a href="/wiki/List_of_LGBT_rights_organizations" title="List of LGBT rights organizations">LGBT associations</a> from <a href="/wiki/2016_High_Level_Meeting_on_Ending_AIDS" title="2016 High Level Meeting on Ending AIDS">2016 High Level Meeting on Ending AIDS</a>, sparking protests by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" title="LGBT community">LGBT communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>The Organization of Islamic Cooperation (OIC) held its <a href="/wiki/OIC_Science_and_Technology_Summit" title="OIC Science and Technology Summit">first science and technology summit</a> at the level of head of state and government in Astana, Republic of Kazakhstan, on 10–11 September 2017.
</p><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Astana_Declaration">Astana Declaration</span></h4>
<p>The Astana Declaration is a policy guidance adopted by OIC members at the Astana Summit. The Astana Declaration commits members to increase investment in science and technology, education, eradicate extreme poverty, and implement UN <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oicdeclaration_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oicdeclaration-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-state_terrorism">Non-state terrorism</span></h3>
<p>In 1999, OIC adopted the OIC Convention on Combatting International Terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Human Rights Watch has noted that the definition of terrorism in article 1 describes "any act or threat of violence carried out with the aim of, among other things, imperiling people’s honour, occupying or seizing public or private property, or threatening the stability, territorial integrity, political unity or sovereignty of a state." HRW views this as vague, ill-defined and including much that is outside the generally accepted understandings of the concept of terrorism. In HRW's view, it labels, or could easily be used to label, as terrorist actions, acts of peaceful expression, association, and assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-terrorism_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terrorism-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Ben_Saul" title="Ben Saul">Ben Saul</a> of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sydney" title="University of Sydney">University of Sydney</a> argues that the definition is subjective and ambiguous and concludes that there is "serious danger of the abusive use of terrorist prosecutions against political opponents" and others.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Furthermore, HRW is concerned by OIC's apparent unwillingness to recognise as terrorism acts that serve causes endorsed by their member states. Article 2 reads: "Peoples' struggle including armed struggle against foreign occupation, aggression, colonialism, and hegemony, aimed at liberation and self-determination." HRW has suggested to OIC that they embrace "longstanding and universally recognised international human rights standards",<sup id="cite_ref-terrorism_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terrorism-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> a request that has as yet not led to any results.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Contradictions between OIC's and other UN members' understanding of terrorism has stymied efforts at the UN to produce a comprehensive convention on international terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During a meeting in Malaysia in April 2002, delegates discussed terrorism but failed to reach a definition of it. They rejected, however, any description of the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Palestinian fight with Israel</a> as terrorism. Their declaration was explicit: "We reject any attempt to link terrorism to the struggle of the Palestinian people in the exercise of their inalienable right to establish their independent state with Al-Quds Al-Shrif (<a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>) as its capital." In fact, at the outset of the meeting, the OIC countries signed a statement praising the Palestinians and their "blessed <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/intifada" class="extiw" title="wikt:intifada">intifada</a>." The word terrorism was restricted to describe Israel, whom they condemned for "<a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a>" in their war with the Palestinian people.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 34th Islamic Conference of Foreign Ministers (ICFM), an OIC section, in May 2007, the foreign ministers termed <a href="/wiki/Islamophobia" title="Islamophobia">Islamophobia</a> "the worst form of terrorism".<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_with_Thailand">Dispute with Thailand</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> has responded to OIC criticism of human rights abuses in the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Thailand" title="Islam in Thailand">Muslim majority</a> provinces of <a href="/wiki/Pattani" class="mw-redirect" title="Pattani">Pattani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yala_Province" title="Yala Province">Yala</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Narathiwat_Province" title="Narathiwat Province">Narathiwat</a> in the south of the country. In a statement issued on 18 October 2005, secretary-general Ihsanoglu vocalised concern over the continuing conflict in the south that "claimed the lives of innocent people and forced the migration of local people out of their places".<sup id="cite_ref-patanipost.com_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patanipost.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> He also stressed that the Thai government's security approach to the crisis would aggravate the situation and lead to continued violence.
</p><p>On 18–19 April 2009, the exiled Patani leader <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abu_Yasir_Fikri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abu Yasir Fikri (page does not exist)">Abu Yasir Fikri</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Patani_United_Liberation_Organisation" title="Patani United Liberation Organisation">Patani United Liberation Organisation</a>) was invited to the OIC to speak about the conflict and present a solution to end the violence between the Thai government and the ethnically Malay Muslims living in the socioeconomically neglected south, that has been struggling against Thai assimilation policy and for self governance since it became annexed by Thailand in 1902. Fikri presented a six-point solution at the conference in Jiddah that included obtaining the same basic rights as other groups when it came to right of language, religion, and culture. He also suggested that Thailand give up its discriminatory policies against the Patani people and allow Patani to at least be allowed the same self-governing rights as other regions in Thailand already have, citing that this does not go against the Thai constitution since it has been done in other parts of Thailand and that it is a matter of political will.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He also criticised the Thai government’s escalation of violence by arming and creating Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militia</a> groups and questioned their intentions. He added Thai policies of not investigating corruption, murder, and human rights violations perpetrated by Bangkok-led administration and military personnel against the Malay Muslim population was an obstacle for achieving peace and healing the deep wounds of being treated as third-class citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thailand responded to this criticism over its policies. The <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thai</a> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kantathi_Suphamongkhon" title="Kantathi Suphamongkhon">Kantathi Suphamongkhon</a>, said: "We have made it clear to the OIC several times that the violence in the deep South is not caused by religious conflict and the government grants protection to all of our citizens no matter what religion they embrace." The Foreign Ministry issued a statement dismissing the OIC’s criticism and accusing it of disseminating misperceptions and misinformation about the situation in the southern provinces. "If the OIC secretariat really wants to promote the cause of peace and harmony in the three southern provinces of Thailand, the responsibility falls on the OIC secretariat to strongly condemn the militants, who are perpetrating these acts of violence against both Thai Muslims and Thai Buddhists."<sup id="cite_ref-patanipost.com_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patanipost.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> HRW<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and Amnesty International<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> have echoed the same concerns as OIC, rebuffing Thailand's attempts to dismiss the issue.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_meetings">Notable meetings</span></h2>
<p>A number of OIC meetings have attracted global attention.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ninth_meeting_of_PUOICM">Ninth meeting of PUOICM</span></h3>
<p>The ninth meeting of Parliamentary Union of the OIC member states (PUOICM) was held on 15 and 16 February 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The speaker of Malaysia's <a href="/wiki/Dewan_Rakyat" title="Dewan Rakyat">House of Representatives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramli_bin_Ngah_Talib" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramli bin Ngah Talib">Ramli bin Ngah Talib</a>, delivered a speech at the beginning of the inaugural ceremony. OIC secretary-general <a href="/wiki/Ekmeleddin_Ihsanoglu" class="mw-redirect" title="Ekmeleddin Ihsanoglu">Ekmeleddin Ihsanoglu</a> said prior to the meeting that one main agenda item was stopping Israel from continuing its excavation at the <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall#Recent_damage_to_plaza" title="Western Wall">Western Wall</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">Al-Aqsa Mosque</a>, Islam's third holiest site.<sup id="cite_ref-mnna_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnna-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The OIC also discussed how it might send peacekeeping troops to Muslim states, as well as the possibility of a change in the name of the body and its charter.<sup id="cite_ref-mnna_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnna-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, return of the sovereignty right to the Iraqi people along with withdrawal of foreign troops from Iraq was another one of the main issues on the agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pakistani Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Khurshid_Mahmud_Kasuri" title="Khurshid Mahmud Kasuri">Khurshid Mahmud Kasuri</a> told reporters on 14 February 2007 that the secretary general of OIC and foreign ministers of seven "like-minded Muslim countries" would meet in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> on 25 February 2007 following meetings of <a href="/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf" title="Pervez Musharraf">President Musharraf</a> with heads of key Muslim countries to discuss "a new initiative" for the resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>. Kasuri said this would be a meeting of foreign ministers of key Muslim countries to discuss and prepare for a summit in <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Makkah Al Mukarramah</a> to seek the resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Arab–Israeli conflict">Arab–Israeli conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IPHRC_Trip_to_Washington_DC">IPHRC Trip to Washington DC</span></h3>
<p>In December 2012, the IPHRC met in Washington, DC for the first time. The IPHRC held meetings at the National Press Club, Capitol Hill and Freedom House discussing the issues of human rights defense in the OIC member states. During their roundtable discussion with Freedom House the IPHRC emphasised the adoption of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights and the rejection of the Cairo Declaration by the OIC.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observer_Status_dispute">Observer Status dispute</span></h3>
<p>The September 2014's high-level Summit of the OIC, in New York, ended without adopting any resolutions or conclusions, for the first time in several years in the modern history of the organization, due to a dispute regarding the status of one of its Observer states. <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> have demanded that the OIC remove the term ‘Turkish Cypriot State’ in reference to the unrecognized <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus">Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus (TRNC)</a>, which has observer status within the organization. Egypt’s president <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a> insisted that any reference to the "Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus or Turkish Cypriot State" was unacceptable and was ultimately the reason for the OIC not adopting any resolutions or conclusions in the 2014 summit.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_and_organisation">Structure and organisation</span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Union_of_the_OIC_Member_States" title="Parliamentary Union of the OIC Member States">Parliamentary Union of the OIC Member States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg/350px-13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg/525px-13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg/700px-13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1960" data-file-height="1075" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:13._Session_of_the_Islamic_Summit_Conference.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Session of the Islamic Summit Conference in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, Turkey, April 2016</div></div></div>
<p>The OIC system consists of:
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_Summit">Islamic Summit</span></h3>
<p>The largest meeting, attended by the kings and the heads of state and government of the member states, convenes every three years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  The Islamic Summit takes policy decisions and provide guidance on all issues pertaining to the realisation of the objectives as provided for in the Charter and consider other issues of concern to the Member States and the Ummah.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_Conference_of_Foreign_Ministers">Islamic Conference of Foreign Ministers</span></h3>
<p>Islamic Conference of Foreign Ministers meets once a year to examine a progress report on the implementation of its decisions taken within the framework of the policy defined by the Islamic Summit.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretary_General">Secretary General</span></h3>
<p>The Secretary General is elected by the Council of Foreign Ministers for a period of five years, renewable once. The Secretary-General is elected from among nationals of the Member States in accordance with the principles of equitable geographical distribution, rotation and equal opportunity for all Member States with due consideration to competence, integrity and experience.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Permanent_Secretariat">Permanent Secretariat</span></h3>
<p>The Permanent Secretariat is the executive organ of the Organisation, entrusted with the implementation of the decisions of the two preceding bodies, and is located in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. The Secretary General of the Organization of Islamic Cooperation (OIC) is Dr. Yousef A. Al-Othaimeen.  He received his office on, Tuesday, 29 November 2016
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiary_organisations">Subsidiary organisations</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Five_Fundamentals_Gate,_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg/220px-Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg/330px-Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg/440px-Five_Fundamentals_Gate%2C_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Five_Fundamentals_Gate,_Islamic_University_of_Technology.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_of_Technology" title="Islamic University of Technology">Islamic University of Technology</a> was set up by the OIC in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Statistical,_Economic_and_Social_Research_and_Training_Centre_for_Islamic_Countries" title="Statistical, Economic and Social Research and Training Centre for Islamic Countries">Statistical, Economic and Social Research and Training Centre for Islamic Countries</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_Centre_for_Islamic_History,_Art_and_Culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Research Centre for Islamic History, Art and Culture (page does not exist)">Research Centre for Islamic History, Art and Culture</a> (IRCICA), located in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_of_Technology" title="Islamic University of Technology">Islamic University of Technology</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Centre_for_the_Development_of_Trade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Centre for the Development of Trade (page does not exist)">Islamic Centre for the Development of Trade</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/International_Islamic_Fiqh_Academy,_Jeddah" title="International Islamic Fiqh Academy, Jeddah">Islamic Fiqh Academy</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamsate_Islamic_Network,_located&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamsate Islamic Network, located (page does not exist)">Islamsate Islamic Network, located</a> at <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Executive_Bureau_of_the_Islamic_Solidarity_Fund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Executive Bureau of the Islamic Solidarity Fund (page does not exist)">Executive Bureau of the Islamic Solidarity Fund</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Waqf" title="Waqf">Waqf</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_in_Niger" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic University in Niger">Islamic University in Niger</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Say,_Niger" title="Say, Niger">Say, Niger</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_in_Uganda" title="Islamic University in Uganda">Islamic University in Uganda</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Mbale" title="Mbale">Mbale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Tabriz_Islamic_Arts_University" title="Tabriz Islamic Arts University">Tabriz Islamic Arts University</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Tabriz" title="Tabriz">Tabriz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialised_institutions">Specialised institutions</span></h3>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Educational,_Scientific_and_Cultural_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organisation">Islamic Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organisation</a> (ISESCO), located in <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_States_Broadcasting_Organisation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic States Broadcasting Organisation (page does not exist)">Islamic States Broadcasting Organisation</a> (ISBO) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Islamic_News_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="International Islamic News Agency">International Islamic News Agency</a> (IINA), located in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliated_institutions">Affiliated institutions</span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Chamber of Commerce and Industry (page does not exist)">Islamic Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a> (ICCI), located in <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, Pakistan.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Islamic_Economic_Forum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="World Islamic Economic Forum (page does not exist)">World Islamic Economic Forum</a> (WIEF), located in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Organisation_of_Islamic_Capitals_and_Cities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Organisation of Islamic Capitals and Cities (page does not exist)">Organisation of Islamic Capitals and Cities</a> (OICC), located in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sports_Federation_of_Islamic_Solidarity_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sports Federation of Islamic Solidarity Games (page does not exist)">Sports Federation of Islamic Solidarity Games</a>, located in Riyadh, Saudi Arabia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Committee_of_the_International_Crescent&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Committee of the International Crescent (page does not exist)">Islamic Committee of the International Crescent</a> (ICIC), located in <a href="/wiki/Benghazi" title="Benghazi">Benghazi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Shipowners_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Shipowners Association (page does not exist)">Islamic Shipowners Association</a> (ISA), located in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Federation_of_International_Arab-Islamic_Schools&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="World Federation of International Arab-Islamic Schools (page does not exist)">World Federation of International Arab-Islamic Schools</a>, located in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Association_of_Islamic_Banks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Association of Islamic Banks (page does not exist)">International Association of Islamic Banks</a> (IAIB), located in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Islamic_Conference_Youth_Forum_for_Dialogue_and_Cooperation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Islamic Conference Youth Forum for Dialogue and Cooperation (page does not exist)">Islamic Conference Youth Forum for Dialogue and Cooperation</a> (ICYF-DC), located in Istanbul, Turkey.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Council_for_Islamic_Banks_and_Financial_Institutions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="General Council for Islamic Banks and Financial Institutions (page does not exist)">General Council for Islamic Banks and Financial Institutions</a> (CIBAFI), located in <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">Manama</a>, Bahrain.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standards_and_Metrology_Institute_for_Islamic_Countries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Standards and Metrology Institute for Islamic Countries (page does not exist)">Standards and Metrology Institute for Islamic Countries</a> (SMIIC), located in Istanbul, Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>
<p>OIC has been criticised by many Muslims for its lack of real engagement and solutions for Muslim countries in crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> It is said to have made progress in social and academic terms but not politically.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
